  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_556ab018-3a6d-4413-8629-c7a7f762c7dd'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1055735722" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3207435938746449144">The Hunger Games: Catching Fire<br/>	In the second book of the Hunger Games series by Suzanne Collins, the main character faces another set of troubles. The group of antagonists, the capitol is as strong as ever but Katniss, the protagonist, is stronger. Katniss has a fiery personality in her relationship with a boy named peeta who was her partner from district 12. Katniss has to work as hard as ever to try to stop the capitol which is under the command of the evil tyrant President Snow who is the re</span>
  <span id="freeText3207435938746449144" style="display:none">The Hunger Games: Catching Fire<br />	In the second book of the Hunger Games series by Suzanne Collins, the main character faces another set of troubles. The group of antagonists, the capitol is as strong as ever but Katniss, the protagonist, is stronger. Katniss has a fiery personality in her relationship with a boy named peeta who was her partner from district 12. Katniss has to work as hard as ever to try to stop the capitol which is under the command of the evil tyrant President Snow who is the reason that the hunger games exist and that the districts four-twelve are such a wreck. In my personal opinion, this book is great for those who desire action. The Hunger games series so far has done a great job of keeping me hooked. When I read this book I can always create an amazing picture in my head of what is going on. The characters in this story are clearly credible in everything they do. There is no magic or fake creatures in the book. Suzanne does a great job of making the book look like it took place in the future while keeping the characters credible. I recommend this book to those of us who often get bored of other books they read or anyone that is preteen or above because of mild action and romance.<br /></span>

          </span>

Catching Fire is a woman's perspective of how the future world may look like. It is a book filled with action and romance. I greatly enjoy the romance between the two protagonist, Peeta and Katniss. I also enjoy reading the action that goes on between the different tributes. Its a great book and very easy to read. Keeps you very interested! </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1943009871&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1943009871" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9709324434095552895">Falling down of the Capital. In “Catching Fire” by Suzanne Collins is about Katniss and Peeta who won the last hunger games in the last book by both threatening president snow by both eating poisonous berries. Through the second book “Catching Fire” it gives the reader what they wanted to know what happened to Katniss and Peeta after the first book. Here's a little of the story and how they got to where they are now. When they got out they were still apart of the hunger games but they didn't kno</span>
  <span id="freeText9709324434095552895" style="display:none">Falling down of the Capital. In “Catching Fire” by Suzanne Collins is about Katniss and Peeta who won the last hunger games in the last book by both threatening president snow by both eating poisonous berries. Through the second book “Catching Fire” it gives the reader what they wanted to know what happened to Katniss and Peeta after the first book. Here's a little of the story and how they got to where they are now. When they got out they were still apart of the hunger games but they didn't know that. President Snow wanted them dead for good this time. Katniss and Peeta started out on a train to go visit districts to red speeches that one of their mentors/ designer have written for them. Katniss had a hard time reading from a script because that's not how she really felt inside. Many people while reading their scripts did the mockingjay symbol and got shot for whoever started it in that district. Katniss was struggling but had to pull through to show that Peeta and her was still in love. While on the train they got told that they would never be free again from the games. So Katniss and Peeta had an idea of getting married so that President snow could realize that they were telling the truth. So later on going through reading the people from previous hunger games got picked from their districts to replay the hunger games. Every person had to show a task or what they could do and Katniss hung a fake mannequin to show that she wasn't scared. So after that the games have started.<br />Katniss was getting ready and as soon as she goes into the tube to go t the arena her designer get beaten and that's the last she saw him before going in the game. Katniss and her allies she picked teamed u but had to fight of and run from some dangerous stuff. What first happened was poisonous fog attacked them in their section on they had to leave behind Mag in order to save Peeta’s life. After that then became a tree that stuck with lighting almost like a clock. So then they got attacked by monkeys and finally made it to the beach where it was safe. So toward the end the partner had an idea of electrocuting the eater so everyone dies but the plan failed and Katniss’s partner Johanna pushed her and cut her wrist. When Katniss was able to move she picked up the wire and aimed it to the dome that they were it. Katniss waited very calmly for the lighting to strike as soon as is stiked she let the air go in the sky or dome that they were put in. The arrow hit the dome ceiling and it started coming down but Katniss was knocked out by the explosion. Katniss then got taken from a big airplane.When Katniss awoke, she got told that they needed to save her to start a revolution. <br />As you can see that this book has many different things going on at once. But it many focuses on Katniss and how she served the 75th hunger games again! Reading this book I started having so many questions but they mostly got answered by the end. I still want to know what happened to Katniss after they took her out of the arena and what did the capital do to Peeta. I think the book could use more detail on what President Snow was doing on his side to give you an idea of what he is capable of doing. Also maybe some more information of what they are going to do to Peeta and how they might cause the revolution Haymitch told Katniss about on the plan. With reading this book I would give it a 8 out of 10 if I were to score it because the lack of information on the enemy's side. To conclude this review, yes I would recommend this book to anyone who likes fiction. <br />	</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2699788015884965349">"Catching Fire" was a very entertaining book that had a wild style. I really enjoyed this book and it kept me on my toes! I read this book in 8th grade but I would recommend this for a high school because of all of the characters and the plot was a little confusing. It was hard for me to keep track of everything and comprehend at the same time. This is why I rated "Catching Fire" a 4 out of 5 stars. Overall "Catching Fire" was a great book and I can't wait to read the rest of the series! </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer910938291886674349"> I believe Suzanne Collins is such a great author because she wrote the book by using "first person" even though I don't like first person that much.<br/><br/> There were multiple themes in this book. There was interdependence vs. independence, loyalty, government control, and rebellion. <br/><br/> Interdependence because this is where Katniss and Peeta mutually depend on each other. Independence because some characters are to act alone freely. Loyalty because during this sequel, they are going to face problems wit</span>
  <span id="freeText910938291886674349" style="display:none"> I believe Suzanne Collins is such a great author because she wrote the book by using "first person" even though I don't like first person that much.<br /><br /> There were multiple themes in this book. There was interdependence vs. independence, loyalty, government control, and rebellion. <br /><br /> Interdependence because this is where Katniss and Peeta mutually depend on each other. Independence because some characters are to act alone freely. Loyalty because during this sequel, they are going to face problems with each other, district, country and their capital. Government control because the government was the one who chose kids and teens to fight during the Hunger Games forcefully. The last theme that I want to say is Rebellion because Katniss has her own thoughts about it ever since the first book and she threatens to commit suicide with Peeta in the last chapter of the first book. In this book Catching Fire, she rebels against the capital's law.<br /><br /> The plot of the book is set after Katniss and Peeta get home from the hunger games. The people who were once friends became enemies, and your enemies are to end up saving you in the end. <br /><br /> I highly recommend this book to everybody who likes romantic,suspense,and action books.I gave this book a 5 star. I gave this book a 5 star because overall I thought that it was so cool that all the Alumni from the different districts came back and fought against each other. This fight was more depressing, and surprising to me.The surprising part in this book is in the end when Katniss shot her arrow towards the sky and it broke/shut down the game. Then, the ship where her trainer, and two other guys who are trying the get revenge on the government picked her up and escaped the game. They took her back to the district, and then Liam told her that there was no District 12 anymore. What will happen now? </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2312935102544469011"> Catching Fire by Suzanne Collins is a fast action novel about a girl named Katniss Everdeen who has fought in the Hunger Games and won, with her lover, Peeta. The sequel of The Hunger Games comes this marvelous novel which has intrigued many readers. Now, Katniss and Peeta have more troubles in their way, although this time, the chances of survival are very low.<br/> Katniss has returned to her new home and has reunited with her family, she has hope that she will also see an old friend as well. She </span>
  <span id="freeText2312935102544469011" style="display:none"> Catching Fire by Suzanne Collins is a fast action novel about a girl named Katniss Everdeen who has fought in the Hunger Games and won, with her lover, Peeta. The sequel of The Hunger Games comes this marvelous novel which has intrigued many readers. Now, Katniss and Peeta have more troubles in their way, although this time, the chances of survival are very low.<br /> Katniss has returned to her new home and has reunited with her family, she has hope that she will also see an old friend as well. She seems to become farther apart from Gale, her peer, which she has not seen since she left for the Hunger Games. Katniss and Peeta are informed that they must participate in the 75th annual Hunger Games. On the way they meet new allies and and enemies. Through the many deaths Katniss saw during both her victory tour and the Hunger games she faces losing close allies Johanna, Enobaria, and lastly Peeta to the Capitol. Gale and Katniss's families are both in danger because of the current violence. Fortunately, Gale was capable of saving them, although District 12 was destroyed.<br /> I thought that this was a great sequel to The Hunger Games because it included many plot twist and Collins fascinating plot. Although, I didn't find this book as compelling as the first. I did love how all of the characters had a purpose and were not just there for the action. My least favorite character is Peeta because I felt as if he was never doing the thing that he's supposed to be doing. He is sweet, but does not take place of his characteristic. It was not until the end of the book were I was truly intrigued. With the complete detail that Collins provided, I was able to imagine all the pieces of the story.<br /> Do read this book, it is a mixture of adventure and violence which continues to tell Katniss's story!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10574411440333793650">This is the second book in the trialgy. It is about Katniss and Peata coming back together to fight for their lives once again. Once they won the first games they were nought they were done fighting. President Snow wants them gone because they are a symbol of hop for the people, so he makes a loop hole that makes returning victors can't me back and fight. Katniss faces many challenges in this book because she and Peata are suppose to be a couple and they have to stick to each other and their all</span>
  <span id="freeText10574411440333793650" style="display:none">This is the second book in the trialgy. It is about Katniss and Peata coming back together to fight for their lives once again. Once they won the first games they were nought they were done fighting. President Snow wants them gone because they are a symbol of hop for the people, so he makes a loop hole that makes returning victors can't me back and fight. Katniss faces many challenges in this book because she and Peata are suppose to be a couple and they have to stick to each other and their allies. Some differences were The Peacekeeper Standoff in District 12<br />In the book, Gale is arrested after attempting to sell a turkey on the black market. In the movie, Gale tackles the new, super-evil Head Peacekeeper to save an old woman in the midst of a full-blown Capitol raid. His punishment for this is getting wiped on his back. Matins, Peata, and Hamitch have to stand up for him and are again resembling hope for the distracts. Another difference is Haymitch, Finnick, Johanna, Beetee, and a handful of other tributes were all working together in order to save Katniss and recruit her for the revolution. The movie makes this clear at the very end, but only gives us a glimpse of Katniss’s reaction (rage, obviously). We don’t watch her spend days in a medicated haze, as we do in the book. We don’t watch her mourn with Finnick; we don’t watch them discuss how their loved ones are better off dead. The movie skips straight to Gale’s announcement that District 12 is no more, and Katniss takes about 30 seconds to go from grief to furious determination.<br /></span>

<div id="review_1266892717" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1266892717" />
    <a title="Christina Martin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42448327-christina-martin"><img alt="Christina Martin" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1266892717?book_show_action=true">Apr 28, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina Martin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina Martin" href="/user/show/42448327-christina-martin">Christina Martin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42448327-christina-martin?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42448327-christina-martin?shelf=fantacy">fantacy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1266892717" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3821874814049691828"><i>Catching Fire</i> is the second book in the <i>Hunger Games<i> series. This book written by Suzanne Collins continues the adventure of the Hunger Game winners Katniss and Peeta. Katniss and Peeta begin their victory tour, only to find out that they must return to the arena and participate in another game. Like the first book, and like the entire series, the reader is kept on their toes constantly wonder what will happen next. The suspense is especially prominent when the main characters are in the game. T</i></i></span>
  <span id="freeText3821874814049691828" style="display:none"><i>Catching Fire</i> is the second book in the <i>Hunger Games<i> series. This book written by Suzanne Collins continues the adventure of the Hunger Game winners Katniss and Peeta. Katniss and Peeta begin their victory tour, only to find out that they must return to the arena and participate in another game. Like the first book, and like the entire series, the reader is kept on their toes constantly wonder what will happen next. The suspense is especially prominent when the main characters are in the game. The concept of children having to fight to the death in these books, in order for society to continue to thrive is very intriguing and disturbing, which is what makes these books so amazing. <i>Catching Fire</i> and the rest of the <i> Hunger Games</i> books are great for middle school students, teenagers in high school, young adults, and adults. Each of these groups will enjoy this book and will not be able to put the book down.</i></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="3821874814049691828" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Fz8Frv4gDgNjk9K0Z7mGjg5kgFSLJuj1ttkmvDhxaIiKK5PXeb3Qx5QT+z7ruE41TbZAquBYC4XnnqEDK0GKCQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

Thomas será mais importante do que imagina. Mas para isso terá de descobrir os sombrias segredos guardados em sua mente e correr... correr muito! <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15671544922605667367"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the Goodreads database with this name.</i><br/><br/>Since 1991, Suzanne Collins has been busy writing for children’s television. She has worked on the staffs of several Nickelodeon shows, including the Emmy-nominated hit Clarissa Explains it All and The Mystery Files of Shelby Woo. For preschool viewers, she penned multiple stories for the Emmy-nominated Little B</span>
  <span id="freeText15671544922605667367" style="display:none"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the Goodreads database with this name.</i><br /><br />Since 1991, Suzanne Collins has been busy writing for children’s television. She has worked on the staffs of several Nickelodeon shows, including the Emmy-nominated hit Clarissa Explains it All and The Mystery Files of Shelby Woo. For preschool viewers, she penned multiple stories for the Emmy-nominated Little Bear and Oswald. She also co-wrote the critically acclaimed Rankin/Bass Christmas special, Santa, Baby! Most recently she was the Head Writer for Scholastic Entertainment’s Clifford’s Puppy Days.<br /><br />While working on a Kids WB show called Generation O! she met children’s author James Proimos, who talked her into giving children’s books a try.<br /><br />Thinking one day about Alice in Wonderland, she was struck by how pastoral the setting must seem to kids who, like her own, lived in urban surroundings. In New York City, you’re much more likely to fall down a manhole than a rabbit hole and, if you do, you’re not going to find a tea party. What you might find...? Well, that’s the story of Gregor the Overlander, the first book in her five-part series, The Underland Chronicles. Suzanne also has a rhyming picture book illustrated by Mike Lester entitled When Charlie McButton Lost Power.<br /><br />She currently lives in Connecticut with her family and a pair of feral kittens they adopted from their backyard.<br /><br />The books she is most successful for in teenage eyes are The Hunger Games, Catching Fire and Mockingjay. These books have won several awards, including the GA Peach Award. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15671544922605667367" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
